You are debugging a production issue in the Naia OS Tauri desktop app (Windows host). I need a root-cause analysis.

## Symptom logs (frontend, all from same session)

```
08:21:58 [legacy-migration] agentAuthLegacyMigrate threw {"error":"legacy-migration timeout after 5000ms","mode":"dev"}
08:21:58 [App] [#337 Phase 8 migration] {"kind":"failed","reason":"legacy-migration timeout after 5000ms"}
08:22:06 [SettingsTab] Lab balance fetch failed {"status":404}
08:43:16 [BgmPlayer] yt search unavailable {"error":"TypeError: Failed to fetch"}
08:43:48 [SettingsTab] [lab-login] opening system browser {"mode":"dev"}
```

## What I have already verified

1. agent process is ALIVE ? `agent-stderr.log` size is stable (no new SyntaxError)
2. `lab_proxy_request` IPC returns (status:404 from portal endpoint) ? **same dispatcher works**
3. `auth_legacy_migrate` IPC times out at 5s ? **specific handler hang**
4. naia.log shows no `Deep link received` entries in recent sessions ? portal already-logged-in ? dashboard, never call
s `naia://auth?...` deep-link

## Hypothesis to verify

`handleAuthLegacyMigrate` calls `saveAuth(state)` ? first-time master-password generation triggers Windows keyring `set
` ? PowerShell + Win32 `CredWrite` P/Invoke spawn takes >5s, exceeding the shell-side 5s timeout in `legacy-migration.t
s`.

The keyring abstraction is at `D:\alpha-adk\projects\naia-agent\packages\runtime\src\utils\keyring.ts` and uses shell-o
ut (PowerShell on Windows).

## Files to inspect

- `D:\alpha-adk\projects\naia-os\shell\src\lib\legacy-migration.ts` (shell-side caller + 5s timeout)
- `D:\alpha-adk\projects\naia-agent\packages\runtime\src\auth\ipc-handlers.ts` (`handleAuthLegacyMigrate`)
- `D:\alpha-adk\projects\naia-agent\packages\runtime\src\utils\auth-store.ts` (`saveAuth`)
- `D:\alpha-adk\projects\naia-agent\packages\runtime\src\utils\keyring.ts` (Windows shell-out path)
- `D:\alpha-adk\projects\naia-os\shell\src-tauri\src\lib.rs` (BGM tsx resolution at `spawn_youtube_bgm_server`, ~line 1
297)

## Your task

Return blunt root-cause analysis with the following structure:

### Primary cause (legacy-migration timeout)
- Where exactly does it hang? Line-precise.
- Is the hypothesis (PowerShell CredWrite spawn) correct? If not, what is?

### Secondary cause (BGM Failed to fetch)
- BGM server at port 18791 dies because lib.rs spawn uses `npx.cmd` fallback, then `'tsx' is not recognized`.
- `naia-os/agent/node_modules/.bin/tsx.CMD` was just installed but the `platform::resolve_tsx_from_agent` only checks `
.pnpm/tsx@*/.../cli.mjs` pattern, not `.bin/`.
- Verify or correct.

### Tertiary (portal deep-link absent)
- Portal already-logged-in redirects to dashboard without firing `naia://auth?...` deep-link. Confirm this is a portal-
side issue or if the OAuth flow has a way to force the callback even on existing session.

### Concrete fixes (ordered by impact)
- Provide actual patches (file:line + diff) for each. Be specific.

Be blunt. The user is frustrated. Quality over diplomacy.

    2: //
    3: // Pure async functions wired into bin/naia-agent.ts stdio dispatcher. Extracted
    4: // from the dispatcher so each handler is independently unit-testable without
    5: // spawning a child process.
    6: //
    7: // Design contract (per design doc 짠2.5):
    8: //   * auth_query / auth_logout / auth_received responses NEVER include the
    9: //     naiaKey ??the whole point of #337 is that the shell never touches it.
   10: //   * lab_proxy_request injects the naiaKey into outbound HTTP headers and
   11: //     returns only the upstream response body, never the key itself.
   12: //   * auth_received + auth_logout are state transitions ??callers also emit
   13: //     `auth_changed` events on stdout (handled in the dispatcher; out of scope
   14: //     for the pure handler).

  102: 	if (req.scope !== undefined) opts.scope = req.scope;
  103: 	if (req.locale !== undefined) opts.locale = req.locale;
  104: 	const { authUrl, state } = startOAuth(opts);
  105: 	return { authUrl, state };

  108: export async function handleAuthReceived(
  109: 	req: AuthReceivedRequest,
  110: ): Promise<AuthReceivedResponse> {
  111: 	const result = await receiveOAuthDeepLink(req.deepLinkUrl);
  112: 	if (!result.ok) {
  113: 		const resp: AuthReceivedResponse = { ok: false };
  114: 		if (result.reason !== undefined) resp.reason = result.reason;
  115: 		return resp;

  118: 	// fields so the shell can correlate (userId, mode) ??never the naiaKey.
  119: 	const resp: AuthReceivedResponse = { ok: true };

  121: 		resp.userId = result.authState.userId;
  122: 		resp.mode = result.authState.mode;
  123: 	}
  124: 	return resp;

  134: export async function handleAuthQuery(
  135: 	req: AuthQueryRequest,
  136: ): Promise<AuthQueryResponse> {
  137: 	const state = await loadAuth(req.mode);
  138: 	if (!state) return { loggedIn: false };
  139: 	// Strip secrets (naiaKey, refreshToken, issuer). Expose only what the shell
  140: 	// needs for UI gating. Phase 7 adds refresh logic; here we always report
  141: 	// loggedIn: true if the file is present ??expiresAt lets the shell warn.
  142: 	const resp: AuthQueryResponse = { loggedIn: true };
  143: 	if (state.expiresAt !== null) resp.expiresAt = state.expiresAt;
  144: 	if (state.userId) resp.userId = state.userId;
  145: 	if (state.scope.length > 0) resp.scope = state.scope.slice();
  146: 	return resp;
  147: }

  149: /**
  150:  * auth_legacy_migrate handler ??one-shot path used by shell Phase 8 to seed
  151:  * the agent's encrypted auth file from the legacy `secure-keys.dat:naiaKey`
  152:  * slot. Matches `auth_received`'s happy-path side effects so the shell never
  153:  * needs to know about the encrypted file directly.
  154:  *
  155:  * Behaviour (design doc 짠3):
  156:  *  * Build a minimal AuthState (refreshToken=null, expiresAt=null, scope=[]).
  157:  *  * Persist via saveAuth ??same as the OAuth deep-link path.
  158:  *  * Return {ok: true} on success; the bin dispatcher is responsible for
  159:  *    emitting the `auth_changed {loggedIn: true}` event.
  160:  *  * On any failure (saveAuth throw / invalid input) return
  161:  *    {ok: false, reason: error.message} ??caller must NOT delete the legacy
  162:  *    slot in that case so the user can retry.
  163:  */
  164: export async function handleAuthLegacyMigrate(
  165: 	req: AuthLegacyMigrateRequest,
  166: ): Promise<AuthLegacyMigrateResponse> {
  167: 	try {
  168: 		if (!req.naiaKey) {
  169: 			return { ok: false, reason: "missing_naia_key" };
  170: 		}
  171: 		const issuer =
  172: 			req.mode === "dev"
  173: 				? "http://localhost:3001"
  174: 				: "https://naia.nextain.io";
  175: 		const now = Math.floor(Date.now() / 1000);
  176: 		const state: AuthState = {
  177: 			schema: 1,
  178: 			keyVersion: 1,
  179: 			mode: req.mode,
  180: 			naiaKey: req.naiaKey,
  181: 			refreshToken: null,
  182: 			userId: req.userId ?? "",
  183: 			issuer,
  184: 			scope: [],
  185: 			issuedAt: now,
  186: 			expiresAt: null,
  187: 			rotatedAt: null,
  188: 		};
  189: 		await saveAuth(state);
  190: 		return { ok: true };
  191: 	} catch (err) {
  192: 		return {
  193: 			ok: false,
  194: 			reason: err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err),
  195: 		};
  196: 	}
  197: }
  198: 
  199: /**
  200:  * lab_proxy_request handler ??issues an authenticated HTTP request on behalf of
  201:  * the shell. The naiaKey is read from the encrypted auth file and injected
  202:  * into the `X-AnyLLM-Key: Bearer ...` header (matches lab-proxy.ts:124-129).
  203:  *
  204:  * Critical: the response NEVER includes the naiaKey in any form. Upstream
  205:  * response body/status are returned as-is; the key is only used to authorize
  206:  * the outbound fetch.
  207:  *
  208:  * Phase 7: on a 401 from the upstream service, attempt a single refresh-token
  209:  * exchange and retry the request once with the rotated naiaKey. Refresh is
  210:  * single-flight per mode (see `refresh.ts`). On refresh failure, the original
  211:  * 401 is returned to the caller and `emit` is invoked with `auth_expired`.
  212:  *
  213:  * `fetchImpl` is injected for testability ??defaults to native fetch.
  214:  * `emit` is injected so the bin dispatcher can route `auth_expired` events to
  215:  * stdout; tests can use a `vi.fn()`.
  216:  */
  217: /**
  218:  * Restrict the proxy to issuer-origin URLs only ??closes the naiaKey
  219:  * exfiltration vector (codex cross-review HIGH #3) where a compromised
  220:  * renderer could pass `path: "https://evil.com/leak"` and the agent would
  221:  * happily inject `X-AnyLLM-Key: Bearer <naiaKey>` into the outbound request.
  222:  *
  223:  * Accepts:
  224:  *   * Route-relative paths starting with "/" (current Phase 6b call-site form)
  225:  *   * Pseudo-absolute URLs whose origin matches the AuthState issuer EXACTLY
  226:  *
  227:  * Rejects everything else (cross-host absolute URLs, malformed URLs,
  228:  * schema-less paths like "api/balance" or "://bogus").
  229:  */
  230: function resolveProxyUrl(reqPath: string, issuer: string): URL {
  231: 	if (reqPath.startsWith("/")) {
  232: 		return new URL(reqPath, issuer);
  233: 	}
  234: 	let parsed: URL;
  235: 	try {
  236: 		parsed = new URL(reqPath);
  237: 	} catch {
  238: 		throw new Error("invalid_path");
  239: 	}
  240: 	const issuerOrigin = new URL(issuer).origin;
  241: 	if (parsed.origin !== issuerOrigin) {
  242: 		throw new Error("disallowed_host");
  243: 	}
  244: 	return parsed;
  245: }
  246: 
  247: export async function handleLabProxyRequest(
  248: 	req: LabProxyRequest,
  249: 	fetchImpl: typeof fetch = fetch,
  250: 	emit?: (event: {
  251: 		type: "auth_expired";
  252: 		mode: AuthMode;
  253: 		reason: RefreshFailureReason;
  254: 	}) => void,
  255: ): Promise<LabProxyResponse> {
  256: 	const state = await loadAuth(req.mode);
  257: 	if (!state) {
  258: 		return { ok: false, status: 401, body: null, error: "not_logged_in" };
  259: 	}
  260: 
  261: 	// Validate the URL BEFORE any fetch call ??never let a compromised renderer
  262: 	// direct the proxy (with naiaKey injection) to an arbitrary host.
  263: 	let url: URL;
  264: 	try {
  265: 		url = resolveProxyUrl(req.path, state.issuer);
  266: 	} catch (err) {
  267: 		const error = err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err);
  268: 		return { ok: false, status: 400, body: null, error };
  269: 	}
  270: 
  271: 	const result = await doFetch(req, state, fetchImpl, url);
  272: 	if (result.status !== 401) return result;
  273: 
  274: 	// 401 ??attempt refresh + retry once.
  275: 	const refreshOpts: Parameters<typeof refreshAuth>[1] = { fetchImpl };
  276: 	if (emit) refreshOpts.emit = emit;
  277: 	const refreshed = await refreshAuth(req.mode, refreshOpts);
  278: 	if (!refreshed.ok || !refreshed.state) {
  279: 		// refreshAuth already emitted auth_expired (when applicable). Surface the
  280: 		// original 401 to the caller so it can pivot to a logged-out UI.
  281: 		return result;
  282: 	}
  283: 	return doFetch(req, refreshed.state, fetchImpl, url);
  284: }
  285: 
  286: async function doFetch(
  287: 	req: LabProxyRequest,
  288: 	state: AuthState,
  289: 	fetchImpl: typeof fetch,
  290: 	url: URL,
  291: ): Promise<LabProxyResponse> {
  292: 	const headers: Record<string, string> = { ...(req.headers ?? {}) };
  293: 	// Override caller's auth header ??shell must never see or set this value.
  294: 	headers["X-AnyLLM-Key"] = `Bearer ${state.naiaKey}`;
  295: 	if (req.body !== undefined && headers["Content-Type"] === undefined) {
  296: 		headers["Content-Type"] = "application/json";
  297: 	}
  298: 
  299: 	let res: Response;
  300: 	try {
  301: 		const init: RequestInit = { method: req.method, headers };
  302: 		if (req.body !== undefined) {
  303: 			init.body = JSON.stringify(req.body);
  304: 		}
  305: 		res = await fetchImpl(url, init);
  306: 	} catch (err) {
  307: 		return {
  308: 			ok: false,
  309: 			status: 0,
  310: 			body: null,
  311: 			error: err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err),
  312: 		};
  313: 	}
  314: 
  315: 	// Parse body ??JSON when content-type allows, plain text otherwise.
  316: 	const contentType = res.headers.get("content-type") ?? "";
  317: 	let body: unknown;
  318: 	try {
  319: 		if (contentType.includes("application/json")) {
  320: 			body = await res.json();
  321: 		} else {
  322: 			body = await res.text();
  323: 		}
  324: 	} catch (err) {
  325: 		body = null;
  326: 		const resp: LabProxyResponse = {
  327: 			ok: false,
  328: 			status: res.status,
  329: 			body: null,
  330: 			error: err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err),
  331: 		};
  332: 		return resp;
  333: 	}
  334: 
  335: 	const resp: LabProxyResponse = {
  336: 		ok: res.status < 400,
  337: 		status: res.status,
  338: 		body,
  339: 	};
  340: 	return resp;
  341: }

    1: // #337 Phase 8 ??one-shot legacy auth migration trigger.
    2: //
    3: // Reads the legacy `secure-keys.dat:naiaKey` slot and pushes it to the
    4: // agent's encrypted `<ADK>/naia-settings/auth/{mode}.json.enc` file via the
    5: // `auth_legacy_migrate` IPC. Designed to run exactly once per process from
    6: // `App.tsx` after the initial auth status query settles (see 짠3 of the
    7: // design doc, `.agents/plans/issue-337-adk-auth-persistence.md`).
    8: //
    9: // Policy (design doc 짠3):
   10: //   1. no legacy key in secure store      ??return early ("nothing to migrate")
   11: //   2. legacy key + agent already logged in ??trust the agent. Silently purge
   12: //      the secure-keys.dat slot (and the stale `apiKey` D3 garbage entry).
   13: //   3. legacy key + agent NOT logged in   ??invoke `auth_legacy_migrate`.
   14: //      Hard-fail on timeout (5 s) or `ok: false`. NO fallback-to-shell ??//      the whole point of #337 is rem
oving dual-SoT. On failure the legacy
   15: //      slot is left intact so the user can retry, and a UI toast event is
   16: //      emitted via `onLegacyMigrationFailed` listeners.
   17: //
   18: // Idempotency: the in-process `migrationPromise` cache makes concurrent calls
   19: // safe ??the second caller awaits the first call's result. After a successful
   20: // migration the legacy key is gone, so a subsequent call hits branch (1).
   21: //
   22: // This module intentionally consumes the `@deprecated getNaiaKeySecure`
   23: // import from `config.ts` ??that's the ONLY remaining shell-side caller and
   24: // will be removed in the Phase 8 wrap-up once telemetry confirms migration
   25: // completion in the field.

   28: 	agentAuthLegacyMigrate,

   39: /** Result discriminant ??surfaced for telemetry + UI toast routing. */
   40: export type LegacyMigrationResult =
   41: 	| { kind: "no_legacy_key" }
   42: 	| { kind: "agent_already_logged_in"; purged: true }
   43: 	| { kind: "migrated"; mode: AuthMode }
   44: 	| { kind: "failed"; reason: string };
   45: 
   46: /** Hard cap on `agentAuthLegacyMigrate` round-trip. Per design 짠3, on timeout
   47:  *  the legacy slot is left intact and a UI toast surfaces so the user can
   48:  *  re-login. */
   49: const MIGRATE_TIMEOUT_MS = 5_000;
   50: 
   51: const failureListeners = new Set<(reason: string) => void>();
   52: let migrationPromise: Promise<LegacyMigrationResult> | null = null;
   53: 
   54: /**
   55:  * Subscribe to migration-failed UI surface events. Returns an unsubscribe
   56:  * function. SettingsTab renders a toast via this listener.
   57:  */
   58: export function onLegacyMigrationFailed(
   59: 	listener: (reason: string) => void,
   60: ): () => void {
   61: 	failureListeners.add(listener);
   62: 	return () => {
   63: 		failureListeners.delete(listener);
   64: 	};
   65: }
   66: 
   67: function emitFailure(reason: string): void {
   68: 	for (const listener of failureListeners) {
   69: 		try {
   70: 			listener(reason);
   71: 		} catch (err) {
   72: 			Logger.warn("legacy-migration", "failure listener threw", {
   73: 				error: String(err),
   74: 			});
   75: 		}
   76: 	}
   77: }
   78: 
   79: /** Wrap a promise with a timeout that rejects with the given message. */
   80: function withTimeout<T>(p: Promise<T>, ms: number, message: string): Promise<T> {
   81: 	return new Promise<T>((resolve, reject) => {
   82: 		const timer = setTimeout(() => reject(new Error(message)), ms);
   83: 		p.then(
   84: 			(value) => {
   85: 				clearTimeout(timer);
   86: 				resolve(value);
   87: 			},
   88: 			(err) => {
   89: 				clearTimeout(timer);
   90: 				reject(err);
   91: 			},
   92: 		);
   93: 	});
   94: }
   95: 
   96: /**
   97:  * Run the one-shot legacy migration. Idempotent ??repeated calls return the
   98:  * cached result of the first call. App.tsx invokes this once on mount after
   99:  * the initial auth status query settles.
  100:  */
  101: export function runLegacyMigration(): Promise<LegacyMigrationResult> {
  102: 	if (!migrationPromise) {
  103: 		migrationPromise = runMigrationOnce();
  104: 	}
  105: 	return migrationPromise;
  106: }
  107: 
  108: async function runMigrationOnce(): Promise<LegacyMigrationResult> {
  109: 	// (1) Pull the legacy key (and userId hint) BEFORE checking the agent so
  110: 	// we don't race a freshly-completed OAuth flow.
  111: 	let legacyKey: string | undefined;
  112: 	try {
  113: 		legacyKey = await getNaiaKeySecure();
  114: 	} catch (err) {
  115: 		Logger.warn("legacy-migration", "getNaiaKeySecure threw", {
  116: 			error: String(err),
  117: 		});
  118: 		legacyKey = undefined;
  119: 	}
  120: 
  121: 	if (!legacyKey) {
  122: 		return { kind: "no_legacy_key" };
  123: 	}
  124: 
  125: 	const localConfig = loadConfig();
  126: 	const legacyUserId =
  127: 		typeof localConfig?.naiaUserId === "string" && localConfig.naiaUserId
  128: 			? localConfig.naiaUserId
  129: 			: undefined;
  130: 	const mode: AuthMode = resolveAuthMode();
  131: 
  132: 	// (2) Check the agent. If it already has the auth file, the legacy slot is
  133: 	// stale ??purge it silently. (Also purge the D3 stale-garbage `apiKey`
  134: 	// slot observed after #329 (B) ??`apiKey: len=7`.)
  135: 	let agentLoggedIn = false;
  136: 	try {
  137: 		const agentState = await agentAuthQuery(mode);
  138: 		agentLoggedIn = agentState.loggedIn;
  139: 	} catch (err) {
  140: 		// Treat IPC failure as "not logged in" defensively ??the migration
  141: 		// attempt will surface a clearer failure path with hard-fail semantics.
  142: 		Logger.warn("legacy-migration", "agentAuthQuery failed", {
  143: 			error: String(err),
  144: 			mode,
  145: 		});
  146: 		agentLoggedIn = false;
  147: 	}
  148: 
  149: 	if (agentLoggedIn) {
  150: 		await deleteSecretKey("naiaKey").catch(() => {});
  151: 		await deleteSecretKey("apiKey").catch(() => {});
  152: 		Logger.info(
  153: 			"legacy-migration",
  154: 			"agent already logged in ??purged legacy slot",
  155: 			{ mode },
  156: 		);
  157: 		return { kind: "agent_already_logged_in", purged: true };
  158: 	}
  159: 
  160: 	// (3) Agent has no auth file ??push the legacy key over. Hard-fail on
  161: 	// timeout or `ok: false` per design doc 짠3.
  162: 	const migrateOpts: Parameters<typeof agentAuthLegacyMigrate>[0] = {
  163: 		mode,
  164: 		naiaKey: legacyKey,
  165: 	};
  166: 	if (legacyUserId !== undefined) migrateOpts.userId = legacyUserId;
  167: 
  168: 	let result: Awaited<ReturnType<typeof agentAuthLegacyMigrate>>;
  169: 	try {
  170: 		result = await withTimeout(
  171: 			agentAuthLegacyMigrate(migrateOpts),
  172: 			MIGRATE_TIMEOUT_MS,
  173: 			`legacy-migration timeout after ${MIGRATE_TIMEOUT_MS}ms`,
  174: 		);
  175: 	} catch (err) {
  176: 		const reason = err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err);
  177: 		Logger.warn("legacy-migration", "agentAuthLegacyMigrate threw", {
  178: 			error: reason,
  179: 			mode,
  180: 		});
  181: 		emitFailure(reason);
  182: 		return { kind: "failed", reason };
  183: 	}
  184: 
  185: 	if (!result.ok) {
  186: 		const reason = result.reason ?? "agent_returned_not_ok";
  187: 		Logger.warn("legacy-migration", "agent returned ok:false", {
  188: 			reason,
  189: 			mode,
  190: 		});
  191: 		emitFailure(reason);
  192: 		return { kind: "failed", reason };
  193: 	}
  194: 
  195: 	// Migration ack OK ??purge the legacy slot + stale-garbage `apiKey` (D3).
  196: 	// The agent's `auth_changed` event has already been emitted on the bin
  197: 	// dispatcher side; the auth-status-store subscriber will flip the badge.
  198: 	await deleteSecretKey("naiaKey").catch(() => {});
  199: 	await deleteSecretKey("apiKey").catch(() => {});
  200: 	Logger.info("legacy-migration", "migrated legacy slot to agent", { mode });
  201: 	return { kind: "migrated", mode };
  202: }

    1: // Encrypted auth-file store for #337 Phase 3.
    2: //
    3: // Persists per-mode bearer tokens at
    4: //   <NAIA_ADK_PATH>/naia-settings/auth/{mode}.json.enc
    5: // using the Phase 2a crypto envelope and the Phase 2b OS-keyring abstraction.
    6: //
    7: // Responsibilities (per design doc 짠2.2 / 짠2.6 / 짠2.9):
    8: //   * Encrypt/decrypt the auth blob with a single per-machine master password
    9: //     stored once in the OS keyring (service "io.nextain.naia",
   10: //     account "auth-master-v1"). First use bootstraps the password.
   11: //   * Atomic writes (`.tmp` + rename) so a mid-write crash never produces a
   12: //     half-written file.
   13: //   * Concurrent readers OK, writers serialized ??implemented with a tiny
   14: //     in-process readers-writer lock keyed by mode. dev/prod are independent.
   15: //   * `mode` resolved from the NAIA_AGENT_MODE env var (default "prod").
   16: //   * Tamper / schema / mode mismatches surface as explicit errors so the
   17: //     caller can react (logout + warn user) rather than silently treating a
   18: //     bad file as "logged out".
   19: //
   20: // Out of scope (deferred to later phases):
   21: //   * Refresh-token rotation + single-flight (Phase 7).
   22: //   * OAuth state generation + deep-link parsing (Phase 4).
   23: //   * Master-key rotation ??`keyVersion` is stored day-1 (cross-review 짠9.4)
   24: //     but only the single value 1 is honored.
   25:

   74: // --- RW lock (per mode) ------------------------------------------------------
   75: 
   76: class RWLock {
   77: 	private readers = 0;
   78: 	private writerActive = false;
   79: 	private waiters: Array<{ kind: "read" | "write"; resolve: () => void }> = [];
   80: 
   81: 	async withRead<T>(fn: () => Promise<T>): Promise<T> {
   82: 		await this.acquireRead();
   83: 		try {
   84: 			return await fn();
   85: 		} finally {
   86: 			this.releaseRead();
   87: 		}
   88: 	}
   89: 
   90: 	async withWrite<T>(fn: () => Promise<T>): Promise<T> {
   91: 		await this.acquireWrite();
   92: 		try {
   93: 			return await fn();
   94: 		} finally {
   95: 			this.releaseWrite();
   96: 		}
   97: 	}
   98: 
   99: 	private acquireRead(): Promise<void> {
  100: 		// Readers wait if a writer is active OR a writer is queued ahead
  101: 		// (fairness ??prevents writer starvation).
  102: 		const writerQueued = this.waiters.some((w) => w.kind === "write");
  103: 		if (!this.writerActive && !writerQueued) {
  104: 			this.readers++;
  105: 			return Promise.resolve();
  106: 		}
  107: 		return new Promise<void>((resolve) => {
  108: 			this.waiters.push({ kind: "read", resolve });
  109: 		});
  110: 	}
  111: 
  112: 	private releaseRead(): void {
  113: 		this.readers--;
  114: 		this.drain();
  115: 	}
  116: 
  117: 	private acquireWrite(): Promise<void> {
  118: 		if (!this.writerActive && this.readers === 0) {
  119: 			this.writerActive = true;
  120: 			return Promise.resolve();
  121: 		}
  122: 		return new Promise<void>((resolve) => {
  123: 			this.waiters.push({ kind: "write", resolve });
  124: 		});
  125: 	}
  126: 
  127: 	private releaseWrite(): void {
  128: 		this.writerActive = false;
  129: 		this.drain();
  130: 	}
  131: 
  132: 	private drain(): void {
  133: 		if (this.writerActive || this.readers > 0) return;
  134: 		const head = this.waiters[0];
  135: 		if (!head) return;
  136: 		if (head.kind === "write") {
  137: 			this.waiters.shift();
  138: 			this.writerActive = true;
  139: 			head.resolve();
  140: 			return;
  141: 		}
  142: 		// Wake all consecutive readers at the head of the queue.
  143: 		while (this.waiters[0]?.kind === "read") {
  144: 			const r = this.waiters.shift()!;
  145: 			this.readers++;
  146: 			r.resolve();
  147: 		}
  148: 	}
  149: }
  150: 
  151: const locks = new Map<AuthMode, RWLock>();
  152: function lockFor(mode: AuthMode): RWLock {
  153: 	let l = locks.get(mode);
  154: 	if (!l) {
  155: 		l = new RWLock();
  156: 		locks.set(mode, l);
  157: 	}
  158: 	return l;
  159: }
  160: 
  161: // --- master password cache ---------------------------------------------------
  162: 
  163: let cachedMasterPassword: string | null = null;
  164: 
  165: async function ensureMasterPassword(): Promise<string> {
  166: 	if (cachedMasterPassword !== null) return cachedMasterPassword;
  167: 	const existing = await getMasterPassword(KEYRING_SERVICE, KEYRING_ACCOUNT);
  168: 	if (existing !== null) {
  169: 		cachedMasterPassword = existing;
  170: 		return existing;
  171: 	}
  172: 	const fresh = generateMasterPassword();
  173: 	await setMasterPassword(KEYRING_SERVICE, KEYRING_ACCOUNT, fresh);
  174: 	cachedMasterPassword = fresh;
  175: 	return fresh;
  176: }
  177: 
  178: // --- atomic write ------------------------------------------------------------
  179: 
  180: // Auth-blob file mode: owner read/write only (0o600). The blob is AES-GCM
  181: // encrypted, but defense-in-depth ??no reason to leave ciphertext readable by
  182: // other local users. Windows: NTFS ignores POSIX mode bits and `fs.chmod` is a
  183: // no-op; default NTFS ACLs are per-user, so the leak is much less severe.
  184: const AUTH_FILE_MODE = 0o600;
  185: const AUTH_DIR_MODE = 0o700;
  186: 
  187: async function atomicWrite(filePath: string, data: Uint8Array): Promise<void> {
  188: 	const tmp = `${filePath}.tmp`;
  189: 	// `writeFile` honors `mode` only on CREATE (open(2) O_CREAT). Pass it so
  190: 	// the temp file starts at 0o600 instead of the umask-derived default.
  191: 	await writeFile(tmp, data, { mode: AUTH_FILE_MODE });
  192: 	await rename(tmp, filePath);
  193: 	// rename(2) preserves the source file's mode, but some filesystems ignore
  194: 	// the `mode` option above. Explicit chmod after rename guarantees the
  195: 	// final state. On Windows this is effectively a no-op.
  196: 	try {
  197: 		await chmod(filePath, AUTH_FILE_MODE);
  198: 	} catch (e) {
  199: 		// A real chmod failure on POSIX is rare (FS without permission bits).
  200: 		// File is still encrypted ??surface as a warning rather than failing
  201: 		// the save. Trade-off: the blob may be group/world-readable.
  202: 		const msg = (e as NodeJS.ErrnoException).message ?? String(e);
  203: 		console.warn(
  204: 			`[auth-store] chmod(${filePath}, 0o600) failed: ${msg} ` +
  205: 				`??file is still encrypted but may be readable by other users.`,
  206: 		);
  207: 	}
  208: }
  209: 
  210: // --- public API --------------------------------------------------------------
  211: 
  212: export async function loadAuth(mode: AuthMode): Promise<AuthState | null> {
  213: 	return lockFor(mode).withRead(async () => {
  214: 		const filePath = getAuthFilePath(mode);
  215: 
  216: 		// File missing ??null (cold boot).
  217: 		let blob: Uint8Array;
  218: 		try {
  219: 			blob = await readFile(filePath);
  220: 		} catch (e) {
  221: 			if ((e as NodeJS.ErrnoException).code === "ENOENT") return null;
  222: 			throw e;
  223: 		}
  224: 
  225: 		// Keyring has no master password ??cannot decrypt. Return null rather
  226: 		// than throwing ??this matches the "no creds available" semantics the
  227: 		// caller expects on fresh installs where the keyring was wiped but a
  228: 		// stale file remained.
  229: 		const existing = await getMasterPassword(KEYRING_SERVICE, KEYRING_ACCOUNT);
  230: 		if (existing === null) return null;
  231: 		cachedMasterPassword = existing;
  232: 
  233: 		const plaintext = await decryptEnvelope(blob, existing);
  234: 		const json = new TextDecoder().decode(plaintext);
  235: 		const parsed = JSON.parse(json) as AuthState;
  236: 
  237: 		if (parsed.schema !== 1) {
  238: 			throw new Error(`Auth file schema mismatch: expected 1, got ${parsed.schema}`);
  239: 		}
  240: 		if (parsed.keyVersion !== 1) {
  241: 			throw new Error(
  242: 				`Auth file keyVersion mismatch: expected 1, got ${parsed.keyVersion}`,
  243: 			);
  244: 		}
  245: 		if (parsed.mode !== mode) {
  246: 			throw new Error(
  247: 				`Auth file mode mismatch: expected ${mode}, got ${parsed.mode}`,
  248: 			);
  249: 		}
  250: 		return parsed;
  251: 	});
  252: }
  253: 
  254: export async function saveAuth(state: AuthState): Promise<void> {
  255: 	const mode = state.mode;
  256: 	return lockFor(mode).withWrite(async () => {
  257: 		const password = await ensureMasterPassword();
  258: 		const filePath = getAuthFilePath(mode);
  259: 		// `mkdir mode` only applies on directory CREATION ??existing dirs keep
  260: 		// their bits. An upgrade path for installs predating this fix is a
  261: 		// separate (LOW) follow-up; file mode is the critical bit. Windows
  262: 		// ignores `mode`.
  263: 		await mkdir(path.dirname(filePath), { recursive: true, mode: AUTH_DIR_MODE });
  264: 
  265: 		const plaintext = new TextEncoder().encode(JSON.stringify(state));
  266: 		const blob = await encryptEnvelope(plaintext, password);
  267: 		await atomicWrite(filePath, blob);
  268: 	});
  269: }
  270: 
  271: export async function deleteAuth(mode: AuthMode): Promise<void> {
  272: 	return lockFor(mode).withWrite(async () => {
  273: 		const filePath = getAuthFilePath(mode);
  274: 		await rm(filePath, { force: true });
  275: 	});
  276: }

  278: // --- test seam ---------------------------------------------------------------
  279: 
  280: /** Reset in-process state (RW locks + cached master password) for isolated
  281:  *  tests. Does NOT touch the keyring or any files on disk. */
  282: export function __resetAuthStoreForTest(): void {
  283: 	locks.clear();
  284: 	cachedMasterPassword = null;
  285: }

 succeeded in 4405ms:
    1: // Cross-platform OS keyring abstraction for the auth master password (#337).
    2: //
    3: // Scope: Phase 2b of issue #337 ??wraps the *native* OS credential store of
    4: // each platform behind a single async interface, plus a documented headless
    5: // fallback when no D-Bus/Keychain is reachable. Used by Phase 3+ to persist
    6: // ONE secret (the auth master password); do not generalize beyond that yet.
    7: //
    8: // Backend choice: shell-out to native CLIs (Option 2).
    9: //   * `keytar` is NOT a dependency of @nextain/agent-runtime and adding a
   10: //     native binding pulls a prebuild toolchain + audit footprint we have
   11: //     deliberately avoided (cf. `secret-store.ts` Slice B rationale).
   12: //   * The existing `secret-store.ts` already shells out to `secret-tool`,
   13: //     so this stays consistent with that precedent.
   14: //   * Per-platform CLIs:
   15: //       - Windows : PowerShell + Windows Credential Manager (CredRead /
   16: //                   CredWrite / CredDelete via Win32 P/Invoke; ships with
   17: //                   every Windows 7+ box).
   18: //       - macOS   : `security` (preinstalled on every macOS).
   19: //       - Linux   : `secret-tool` (libsecret; same backend as secret-store).
   20: //
   21: // Headless fallback:
   22: //   When all native backends report unavailable (no D-Bus session, libsecret
   23: //   missing, etc.), we derive a deterministic key from
   24: //     SHA256( machine-id || user-uid-or-name || "naia-headless-fallback-v1" )
   25: //   and use it as the *stored password*. This is consistent across restarts
   26: //   for the same machine + user ??the auth-persistence requirement ??but is
   27: //   NOT cryptographically secure against a local attacker with file-read
   28: //   access (machine-id is world-readable on Linux). The caller is warned via
   29: //   a one-shot console.warn so the user can choose to fix their environment
   30: //   (start dbus, install libsecret-tools, log into a graphical session, ??.
   31: //
   32: // This module deliberately does NOT depend on `crypto-envelope.ts` (Phase 2a)
   33: // ??Phase 3 wires them together.
   34: 
   35: import { spawnSync, type SpawnSyncReturns } from "node:child_process";
   36: import { createHash } from "node:crypto";
   37: import { readFileSync, writeFileSync } from "node:fs";
   38: import { userInfo } from "node:os";
   39: 
   40: export type KeyringBackendName = "windows" | "macos" | "linux" | "headless";
   41: 
   42: export interface KeyringBackend {
   43: 	name: KeyringBackendName;
   44: 	isAvailable(): Promise<boolean>;
   45: 	set(service: string, account: string, password: string): Promise<void>;
   46: 	get(service: string, account: string): Promise<string | null>;
   47: 	delete(service: string, account: string): Promise<void>;
   48: }
   49: 
   50: // --- internal test seams -----------------------------------------------------
   51: 
   52: /** Indirection so tests can simulate other platforms / fake `exec`. */
   53: export interface KeyringEnvironment {
   54: 	platform: NodeJS.Platform;
   55: 	/** Spawn a process synchronously; mirrors child_process.spawnSync output. */
   56: 	exec(
   57: 		cmd: string,
   58: 		args: string[],
   59: 		opts?: { input?: string; timeoutMs?: number },
   60: 	): SpawnSyncReturns<string>;
   61: 	/** Read a file as utf8; returns null if missing/unreadable. */
   62: 	readTextFile(path: string): string | null;
   63: 	/** os.userInfo() ??returns just the fields we use. */
   64: 	userInfo(): { uid: number; username: string };
   65: }
   66: 
   67: const DEFAULT_ENV: KeyringEnvironment = {
   68: 	platform: process.platform,
   69: 	exec(cmd, args, opts) {
   70: 		return spawnSync(cmd, args, {
   71: 			encoding: "utf8",
   72: 			timeout: opts?.timeoutMs ?? 5000,
   73: 			...(opts?.input !== undefined ? { input: opts.input } : {}),
   74: 		});
   75: 	},
   76: 	readTextFile(path) {
   77: 		try {
   78: 			return readFileSync(path, "utf8");
   79: 		} catch {
   80: 			return null;
   81: 		}
   82: 	},
   83: 	userInfo() {
   84: 		const u = userInfo();
   85: 		return { uid: u.uid, username: u.username };
   86: 	},
   87: };

   89: // --- Linux backend (secret-tool / libsecret) ---------------------------------
   90: 
   91: function makeLinuxBackend(env: KeyringEnvironment): KeyringBackend {
   92: 	// Force C locale: any stderr inspection stays deterministic across boxes.
   93: 	const ENV_VARS = { LC_ALL: "C", LANG: "C", LANGUAGE: "C" };
   94: 	const PROBE_ACCOUNT = "__naia_keyring_probe_absent__";
   95: 	const PROBE_SERVICE = "naia-agent-keyring-probe";
   96: 
   97: 	function classify(r: SpawnSyncReturns<string>): "found" | "absent" | "broken" {
   98: 		if (r.error || r.status === null) return "broken";
   99: 		if (r.status === 0) return "found";
  100: 		if (r.status === 1 && (r.stderr ?? "").trim() === "") return "absent";
  101: 		return "broken";
  102: 	}
  103: 
  104: 	let cached: boolean | undefined;
  105: 	return {
  106: 		name: "linux",
  107: 		async isAvailable() {
  108: 			if (cached !== undefined) return cached;
  109: 			const r = env.exec(
  110: 				"secret-tool",
  111: 				["lookup", "service", PROBE_SERVICE, "account", PROBE_ACCOUNT],
  112: 				{ timeoutMs: 5000 },
  113: 			);
  114: 			// Carry locale env via a wrapper since we can't pass env through our
  115: 			// minimal exec seam ??secret-tool error text is what we classify.
  116: 			// (We rely on classifyProbe's stderr-empty check, which is locale-
  117: 			//  independent for the healthy "absent key" case.)
  118: 			const c = classify(r);
  119: 			cached = c === "found" || c === "absent";
  120: 			// Reference ENV_VARS so unused-var linting stays quiet without
  121: 			// changing the seam shape. (Real env is inherited from parent.)
  122: 			void ENV_VARS;
  123: 			return cached;
  124: 		},
  125: 		async set(service, account, password) {
  126: 			const r = env.exec(
  127: 				"secret-tool",
  128: 				["store", "--label", `${service}: ${account}`, "service", service, "account", account],
  129: 				{ input: password, timeoutMs: 5000 },
  130: 			);
  131: 			if (r.error || r.status !== 0) {
  132: 				throw new Error(
  133: 					`secret-tool store failed (status=${r.status ?? "null"}): ${(r.stderr ?? "").trim()}`,
  134: 				);
  135: 			}
  136: 		},
  137: 		async get(service, account) {
  138: 			const r = env.exec(
  139: 				"secret-tool",
  140: 				["lookup", "service", service, "account", account],
  141: 				{ timeoutMs: 5000 },
  142: 			);
  143: 			const c = classify(r);
  144: 			if (c === "found") {
  145: 				const out = r.stdout ?? "";
  146: 				return out.length > 0 ? out.replace(/\n$/, "") : null;
  147: 			}
  148: 			if (c === "absent") return null;
  149: 			throw new Error(
  150: 				`secret-tool lookup failed (status=${r.status ?? "null"}): ${(r.stderr ?? "").trim()}`,
  151: 			);
  152: 		},
  153: 		async delete(service, account) {
  154: 			const r = env.exec(
  155: 				"secret-tool",
  156: 				["clear", "service", service, "account", account],
  157: 				{ timeoutMs: 5000 },
  158: 			);
  159: 			// secret-tool clear exits 0 whether the entry existed or not; only
  160: 			// fail loudly when the binary itself crashed.
  161: 			if (r.error || r.status === null) {
  162: 				throw new Error(`secret-tool clear failed: ${(r.stderr ?? "").trim()}`);
  163: 			}
  164: 		},
  165: 	};
  166: }

  168: // --- macOS backend (`security` CLI) ------------------------------------------
  169: 
  170: function makeMacosBackend(env: KeyringEnvironment): KeyringBackend {
  171: 	let cached: boolean | undefined;
  172: 	return {
  173: 		name: "macos",
  174: 		async isAvailable() {
  175: 			if (cached !== undefined) return cached;
  176: 			// `security` is preinstalled; treat "missing binary" as unavailable.
  177: 			// `-h` exits 0 on every shipped macOS.
  178: 			const r = env.exec("security", ["-h"], { timeoutMs: 3000 });
  179: 			cached = !r.error && r.status !== null;
  180: 			return cached;
  181: 		},
  182: 		async set(service, account, password) {
  183: 			// `-U` updates if exists; without it `add-generic-password` errors
  184: 			// with status 45 (errSecDuplicateItem).
  185: 			//
  186: 			// Codex cross-review finding #4 (HIGH): the master password MUST NOT
  187: 			// be passed as an argv element. Per `man security(1)`, when the
  188: 			// `-w` flag is supplied with NO trailing value, the password is
  189: 			// read from stdin (one line) ??keeping it out of `/proc/<pid>/argv`
  190: 			// and out of process-inspection tools like `ps` / `top` / `htop`.
  191: 			// Escape hatch: `NAIA_KEYRING_MACOS_LEGACY_ARGV=1` reverts to the
  192: 			// old argv-based path for any user who hits an edge case (e.g. a
  193: 			// hypothetical legacy `security` that doesn't honor stdin `-w`).
  194: 			// This is documented to leak the password and should only be used
  195: 			// as a temporary diagnostic.
  196: 			const legacy = process.env.NAIA_KEYRING_MACOS_LEGACY_ARGV === "1";
  197: 			const r = legacy
  198: 				? env.exec(
  199: 					"security",
  200: 					[
  201: 						"add-generic-password",
  202: 						"-U",
  203: 						"-s", service,
  204: 						"-a", account,
  205: 						"-w", password,
  206: 					],
  207: 					{ timeoutMs: 5000 },
  208: 				)
  209: 				: env.exec(
  210: 					"security",
  211: 					[
  212: 						"add-generic-password",
  213: 						"-U",
  214: 						"-s", service,
  215: 						"-a", account,
  216: 						"-w",
  217: 					],
  218: 					{ input: password, timeoutMs: 5000 },
  219: 				);
  220: 			if (r.error || r.status !== 0) {
  221: 				throw new Error(
  222: 					`security add-generic-password failed (status=${r.status ?? "null"}): ${(r.stderr ?? "").trim()}`,
  223: 				);
  224: 			}
  225: 		},
  226: 		async get(service, account) {
  227: 			// `-w` prints just the password on stdout. Status 44 = item not found.
  228: 			const r = env.exec(
  229: 				"security",
  230: 				["find-generic-password", "-s", service, "-a", account, "-w"],
  231: 				{ timeoutMs: 5000 },
  232: 			);
  233: 			if (r.status === 0) {
  234: 				const out = r.stdout ?? "";
  235: 				return out.length > 0 ? out.replace(/\n$/, "") : null;
  236: 			}
  237: 			if (r.status === 44) return null;
  238: 			throw new Error(
  239: 				`security find-generic-password failed (status=${r.status ?? "null"}): ${(r.stderr ?? "").trim()}`,
  240: 			);
  241: 		},
  242: 		async delete(service, account) {
  243: 			const r = env.exec(
  244: 				"security",
  245: 				["delete-generic-password", "-s", service, "-a", account],
  246: 				{ timeoutMs: 5000 },
  247: 			);
  248: 			// Idempotent: status 44 = not found is OK.
  249: 			if (r.status === 0 || r.status === 44) return;
  250: 			if (r.error || r.status === null) {
  251: 				throw new Error(`security delete-generic-password failed: ${(r.stderr ?? "").trim()}`);
  252: 			}
  253: 			throw new Error(
  254: 				`security delete-generic-password failed (status=${r.status}): ${(r.stderr ?? "").trim()}`,
  255: 			);
  256: 		},
  257: 	};
  258: }

  267: const WIN_PS_HELPER = `
  268: $Sig = @'
  269: using System;
  270: using System.Runtime.InteropServices;
  271: using System.Text;
  272: public static class Cred {
  273:   [StructLayout(LayoutKind.Sequential, CharSet = CharSet.Unicode)]
  274:   public struct CREDENTIAL {
  275:     public UInt32 Flags; public UInt32 Type; public IntPtr TargetName;
  276:     public IntPtr Comment; public System.Runtime.InteropServices.ComTypes.FILETIME LastWritten;
  277:     public UInt32 CredentialBlobSize; public IntPtr CredentialBlob;
  278:     public UInt32 Persist; public UInt32 AttributeCount; public IntPtr Attributes;
  279:     public IntPtr TargetAlias; public IntPtr UserName;
  280:   }
  281:   [DllImport("advapi32.dll", EntryPoint="CredReadW", CharSet=CharSet.Unicode, SetLastError=true)]
  282:   public static extern bool CredRead(string target, UInt32 type, UInt32 reservedFlag, out IntPtr credentialPtr);
  283:   [DllImport("advapi32.dll", EntryPoint="CredWriteW", CharSet=CharSet.Unicode, SetLastError=true)]
  284:   public static extern bool CredWrite(ref CREDENTIAL credential, UInt32 flags);
  285:   [DllImport("advapi32.dll", EntryPoint="CredDeleteW", CharSet=CharSet.Unicode, SetLastError=true)]
  286:   public static extern bool CredDelete(string target, UInt32 type, UInt32 flags);
  287:   [DllImport("advapi32.dll", SetLastError=true)]
  288:   public static extern void CredFree(IntPtr cred);
  289: }

  293: 
  294: function makeWindowsBackend(env: KeyringEnvironment): KeyringBackend {
  295: 	let cached: boolean | undefined;
  296: 
  297: 	function runPS(script: string, input?: string): SpawnSyncReturns<string> {
  298: 		const full = `${WIN_PS_HELPER}\n${script}`;
  299: 		return env.exec(
  300: 			"powershell",
  301: 			["-NoProfile", "-NonInteractive", "-ExecutionPolicy", "Bypass", "-Command", full],
  302: 			input !== undefined ? { input, timeoutMs: 10000 } : { timeoutMs: 10000 },
  303: 		);
  304: 	}
  305: 
  306: 	function target(service: string, account: string): string {
  307: 		return `${service}:${account}`;
  308: 	}

  318:   if ($p -ne [IntPtr]::Zero) { [Cred]::CredFree($p) }

  352: if (-not $ok) {
  353:   $err = [System.Runtime.InteropServices.Marshal]::GetLastWin32Error()
  354:   if ($err -eq 1168) { Write-Output 'NOTFOUND'; exit 0 }

  372: 				return Buffer.from(out.slice(4), "base64").toString("utf8");
  373: 			}

  392: // --- Headless fallback -------------------------------------------------------
  393: 
  394: const HEADLESS_SALT = "naia-headless-fallback-v1";
  395: const HEADLESS_WARNING =
  396: 	"[naia-agent] WARNING: OS keyring unavailable, using machine-id fallback. " +
  397: 	"Auth files have degraded protection.";
  398: 
  399: // Module-level latch ??warn once per process, even across multiple keyring
  400: // instances. Cleared by the test seam below.
  401: let headlessWarned = false;
  402: 
  403: export function __resetHeadlessWarnedForTest(): void {
  404: 	headlessWarned = false;
  405: }
  406: 
  407: function readMachineId(env: KeyringEnvironment): string {
  408: 	if (env.platform === "linux") {
  409: 		return (
  410: 			env.readTextFile("/etc/machine-id")?.trim() ??
  411: 			env.readTextFile("/var/lib/dbus/machine-id")?.trim() ??
  412: 			"linux-no-machine-id"
  413: 		);
  414: 	}
  415: 	if (env.platform === "darwin") {
  416: 		const r = env.exec("ioreg", ["-rd1", "-c", "IOPlatformExpertDevice"], { timeoutMs: 3000 });
  417: 		if (!r.error && r.status === 0) {
  418: 			const m = /"IOPlatformUUID"\s*=\s*"([^"]+)"/.exec(r.stdout ?? "");
  419: 			if (m && m[1]) return m[1];
  420: 		}
  421: 		return "darwin-no-uuid";
  422: 	}
  423: 	if (env.platform === "win32") {
  424: 		// HKLM\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Cryptography\MachineGuid ??stable per install.
  425: 		const r = env.exec(
  426: 			"reg",
  427: 			["query", "HKLM\\SOFTWARE\\Microsoft\\Cryptography", "/v", "MachineGuid"],
  428: 			{ timeoutMs: 3000 },
  429: 		);
  430: 		if (!r.error && r.status === 0) {
  431: 			const m = /MachineGuid\s+REG_SZ\s+([0-9a-fA-F-]+)/.exec(r.stdout ?? "");
  432: 			if (m && m[1]) return m[1];
  433: 		}
  434: 		return "win32-no-machineguid";
  435: 	}
  436: 	return `${env.platform}-no-id`;
  437: }
  438: 
  439: function deriveHeadlessKey(env: KeyringEnvironment): string {
  440: 	const machineId = readMachineId(env);
  441: 	const u = env.userInfo();
  442: 	// uid is -1 on Windows; prefer username there. On Unix uid is stable.
  443: 	const userPart = env.platform === "win32" ? u.username : String(u.uid);
  444: 	const h = createHash("sha256");
  445: 	h.update(machineId);
  446: 	h.update("\0");
  447: 	h.update(userPart);
  448: 	h.update("\0");
  449: 	h.update(HEADLESS_SALT);
  450: 	return h.digest("hex");
  451: }
  452: 
  453: function makeHeadlessBackend(env: KeyringEnvironment): KeyringBackend {
  454: 	// Per-process in-memory map: callers may set() a different value than the
  455: 	// derived key (e.g. an actual master password the user typed). The derived
  456: 	// key is the *default* returned on a cold get() when nothing was stored,
  457: 	// which is what gives us cross-restart auth persistence.
  458: 	const overrides = new Map<string, string>();
  459: 	function key(service: string, account: string) {
  460: 		return `${service} ${account}`;
  461: 	}
  462: 	function warnOnce(): void {
  463: 		if (headlessWarned) return;
  464: 		headlessWarned = true;
  465: 		// eslint-disable-next-line no-console
  466: 		console.warn(HEADLESS_WARNING);
  467: 	}
  468: 	return {
  469: 		name: "headless",
  470: 		async isAvailable() {
  471: 			return true; // always usable, by definition of the fallback
  472: 		},
  473: 		async set(service, account, password) {
  474: 			warnOnce();
  475: 			overrides.set(key(service, account), password);
  476: 		},
  477: 		async get(service, account) {
  478: 			warnOnce();
  479: 			const k = key(service, account);
  480: 			if (overrides.has(k)) return overrides.get(k) ?? null;
  481: 			return deriveHeadlessKey(env);
  482: 		},
  483: 		async delete(service, account) {
  484: 			warnOnce();
  485: 			overrides.delete(key(service, account)); // idempotent
  486: 		},
  487: 	};
  488: }
  489: 
  490: // --- file-backed test backend (cross-process integration tests) -------------
  491: 
  492: // Persists a JSON `{ "service account": "password" }` map to the path in
  493: // `NAIA_KEYRING_TEST_FILE`. Used ONLY by integration tests that spawn child
  494: // agent processes (#337 Phase 10 S115/S116) where a memory-only stub cannot
  495: // survive the spawn boundary and the real OS keyring would pollute user state.
  496: //
  497: // NEVER selected unless the env var is set ??keeps production paths untouched.
  498: 
  499: function makeFileBackedTestBackend(filePath: string): KeyringBackend {
  500: 	function load(): Map<string, string> {
  501: 		try {
  502: 			const raw = readFileSync(filePath, "utf8");
  503: 			const obj = JSON.parse(raw) as Record<string, string>;
  504: 			return new Map(Object.entries(obj));
  505: 		} catch {
  506: 			return new Map();
  507: 		}
  508: 	}
  509: 	function save(m: Map<string, string>): void {
  510: 		const obj: Record<string, string> = {};
  511: 		for (const [k, v] of m) obj[k] = v;
  512: 		writeFileSync(filePath, JSON.stringify(obj));
  513: 	}
  514: 	const k = (service: string, account: string) => `${service} ${account}`;
  515: 	return {
  516: 		name: "headless",
  517: 		async isAvailable() {
  518: 			return true;
  519: 		},
  520: 		async set(service, account, password) {
  521: 			const m = load();
  522: 			m.set(k(service, account), password);
  523: 			save(m);
  524: 		},
  525: 		async get(service, account) {
  526: 			const m = load();
  527: 			return m.get(k(service, account)) ?? null;
  528: 		},
  529: 		async delete(service, account) {
  530: 			const m = load();
  531: 			m.delete(k(service, account));
  532: 			save(m);
  533: 		},
  534: 	};
  535: }
  536: 
  537: // --- selection logic ---------------------------------------------------------
  538: 
  539: async function selectBackend(env: KeyringEnvironment): Promise<KeyringBackend> {
  540: 	// Test seam: cross-process file-backed backend. Selected only when the env
  541: 	// var is set; production code paths never see this branch.
  542: 	const testFile = process.env.NAIA_KEYRING_TEST_FILE;
  543: 	if (testFile) return makeFileBackedTestBackend(testFile);
  544: 
  545: 	let native: KeyringBackend | null = null;
  546: 	if (env.platform === "win32") native = makeWindowsBackend(env);
  547: 	else if (env.platform === "darwin") native = makeMacosBackend(env);
  548: 	else if (env.platform === "linux") native = makeLinuxBackend(env);
  549: 
  550: 	if (native && (await native.isAvailable())) return native;
  551: 	return makeHeadlessBackend(env);
  552: }

    1: // OAuth flow handler for #337 Phase 4.
    2: //
    3: // Pure-function module + in-memory state manager. Phase 5 wires this to shell
    4: // IPC. Responsibilities (per design doc 짠2.5 / 짠2.7):
    5: //
    6: //   * Generate OAuth state tokens (32-byte hex) with mode/issuer/scope binding
    7: //     and a 5-minute TTL, in-memory only ??no disk persistence (a crashed
    8: //     agent forces re-login, identical to current shell behavior, 짠8 Q3).
    9: //   * Build the Naia portal login URL with state embedded.
   10: //   * Parse incoming `naia://auth?...` deep-link URLs, validate state, and
   11: //     persist the resulting bearer token via auth-store.saveAuth().
   12: //   * Maintain a forensic in-memory log of every deep-link receive event ??//     success and reject both logge
d ??for security forensics (짠2.7).
   13: //
   14: // Out of scope by design:
   15: //   * PKCE ??deferred to a portal-side follow-up issue (짠2.7 / 짠9.5). The
   16: //     current portal returns naiaKey directly in `naia://auth?key=...`; we
   17: //     honor that flow with stronger state validation + TTL.
   18: //   * Shell IPC wiring ??Phase 5 picks that up; this module only exposes the
   19: //     pure functions Phase 5 will call.
   20: 
   21: import { randomBytes } from "node:crypto";
   22: 
   23: import { type AuthMode, type AuthState, saveAuth } from "./auth-store.js";
   24: 
   25: // --- public types ------------------------------------------------------------
   26: 
   27: export interface OAuthStartOptions {
   28: 	mode: AuthMode;
   29: 	/** Override portal base URL ??defaults to mode-derived issuer. */
   30: 	issuerOverride?: string;
   31: 	/** Requested scopes ??opaque strings, passed to portal as comma-separated
   32: 	 *  `scope=` query. Empty array ??no `scope=` param emitted. */
   33: 	scope?: string[];
   34: 	/** Locale segment for portal URL (e.g. "ko", "en"). Default "en". */
   35: 	locale?: string;
   36: }
   37: 
   38: export interface OAuthStartResult {
   39: 	/** Full URL to open in webview. */
   40: 	authUrl: string;
   41: 	/** State token (caller should not store ??it's already in-memory in this
   42: 	 *  module). Exposed mainly for tests + log correlation. */
   43: 	state: string;
   44: }
   45: 
   46: export type OAuthRejectReason =
   47: 	| "missing_state"
   48: 	| "unknown_state"
   49: 	| "expired_state"
   50: 	| "mode_mismatch"
   51: 	| "missing_key"
   52: 	| "malformed_url";
   53: 
   54: export interface OAuthReceiveResult {
   55: 	ok: boolean;
   56: 	reason?: OAuthRejectReason;
   57: 	authState?: AuthState; // populated on ok:true
   58: }
   59: 
   60: export interface OAuthLogEntry {
   61: 	timestamp: number; // unix ms
   62: 	event: "start" | "receive_success" | "receive_reject";
   63: 	reason?: OAuthRejectReason;
   64: 	mode?: AuthMode;
   65: 	state?: string; // OK to log ??short-lived, already used
   66: 	userId?: string; // OK on success
   67: 	// NEVER log naiaKey or any secret.
   68: }
   69: 
   70: // --- constants ---------------------------------------------------------------
   71: 
   72: const STATE_TTL_MS = 5 * 60 * 1000; // 5 minutes
   73: const LOG_BUFFER_CAP = 1000;
   74: 
   75: // --- issuer URL resolution ---------------------------------------------------
   76: 
   77: function resolveIssuer(mode: AuthMode, override?: string): string {
   78: 	if (override) return override;
   79: 	return mode === "dev" ? "http://localhost:3001" : "https://naia.nextain.io";
   80: }
   81: 
   82: // --- in-memory state map -----------------------------------------------------
   83: 
   84: interface BoundState {
   85: 	mode: AuthMode;
   86: 	issuer: string;
   87: 	scope: string[];
   88: 	expiresAt: number; // unix ms
   89: }
   90: 
   91: const stateMap = new Map<string, BoundState>();
   92: 
   93: // --- forensic log ------------------------------------------------------------
   94: 
   95: const logBuffer: OAuthLogEntry[] = [];
   96: const logListeners = new Set<(entry: OAuthLogEntry) => void>();
   97: 
   98: function appendLog(entry: OAuthLogEntry): void {
   99: 	logBuffer.push(entry);
  100: 	if (logBuffer.length > LOG_BUFFER_CAP) {
  101: 		logBuffer.shift();
  102: 	}
  103: 	for (const listener of logListeners) {
  104: 		try {
  105: 			listener(entry);
  106: 		} catch {
  107: 			// Subscribers must not crash the flow. Swallow silently ??the buffer
  108: 			// itself is the durable record.
  109: 		}
  110: 	}
  111: }
  112: 
  113: // --- public API --------------------------------------------------------------
  114: 
  115: /** Begin an OAuth flow. Generates a state token, stores it with 5-min TTL,
  116:  *  returns the URL the shell should open in a webview. */
  117: export function startOAuth(opts: OAuthStartOptions): OAuthStartResult {
  118: 	const mode = opts.mode;
  119: 	const issuer = resolveIssuer(mode, opts.issuerOverride);
  120: 	const scope = opts.scope ?? [];
  121: 	const locale = opts.locale ?? "en";
  122: 
  123: 	const state = randomBytes(32).toString("hex");
  124: 	stateMap.set(state, {
  125: 		mode,
  126: 		issuer,
  127: 		scope,
  128: 		expiresAt: Date.now() + STATE_TTL_MS,
  129: 	});
  130: 
  131: 	const params = new URLSearchParams();
  132: 	if (scope.length > 0) params.set("scope", scope.join(","));
  133: 	params.set("state", state);
  134: 	params.set("app", "naia-os");
  135: 	params.set("platform", process.platform);
  136: 	const authUrl = `${issuer}/${locale}/login?${params.toString()}`;
  137: 
  138: 	appendLog({
  139: 		timestamp: Date.now(),
  140: 		event: "start",
  141: 		mode,
  142: 		state,
  143: 	});
  144: 
  145: 	return { authUrl, state };
  146: }
  147: 
  148: /** Parse a naia://auth?... deep-link URL. Validates state, persists AuthState
  149:  *  via saveAuth(), returns result. Forensic log emitted regardless of outcome
  150:  *  (success + failure both logged). */
  151: export async function receiveOAuthDeepLink(
  152: 	deepLinkUrl: string,
  153: ): Promise<OAuthReceiveResult> {
  154: 	// naia:// is not in WHATWG's special-scheme list, so query parsing via the
  155: 	// standard URL constructor on the raw scheme is unreliable across
  156: 	// implementations. Substitute the scheme with https:// for parsing only ??	// we never use the resulting URL b
eyond extracting query params.
  157: 	let parsed: URL;
  158: 	try {
  159: 		parsed = new URL(deepLinkUrl.replace(/^naia:\/\//, "https://"));
  160: 	} catch {
  161: 		return reject("malformed_url");
  162: 	}
  163: 
  164: 	const params = parsed.searchParams;
  165: 	const stateParam = params.get("state");
  166: 	if (!stateParam) return reject("missing_state");
  167: 
  168: 	const bound = stateMap.get(stateParam);
  169: 	if (!bound) return reject("unknown_state", undefined, stateParam);
  170: 
  171: 	// Single-use: remove from map immediately. Subsequent receives with the
  172: 	// same state will fall into the unknown_state branch above.
  173: 	stateMap.delete(stateParam);
  174: 
  175: 	if (Date.now() > bound.expiresAt) {
  176: 		return reject("expired_state", bound.mode, stateParam);
  177: 	}
  178: 
  179: 	const keyParam = params.get("key");
  180: 	if (!keyParam) return reject("missing_key", bound.mode, stateParam);
  181: 
  182: 	const userIdParam = params.get("user_id") ?? "";
  183: 	const refreshTokenParam = params.get("refresh_token");
  184: 	const expiresAtParam = params.get("expires_at");
  185: 	const scopeParam = params.get("scope");
  186: 
  187: 	const now = Math.floor(Date.now() / 1000);
  188: 	const authState: AuthState = {
  189: 		schema: 1,
  190: 		keyVersion: 1,
  191: 		mode: bound.mode,
  192: 		naiaKey: keyParam,
  193: 		refreshToken: refreshTokenParam ?? null,
  194: 		userId: userIdParam,
  195: 		issuer: bound.issuer,
  196: 		scope: scopeParam ? scopeParam.split(",") : bound.scope,
  197: 		issuedAt: now,
  198: 		expiresAt: expiresAtParam ? Number(expiresAtParam) : null,
  199: 		rotatedAt: null,
  200: 	};
  201: 
  202: 	await saveAuth(authState);
  203: 
  204: 	appendLog({
  205: 		timestamp: Date.now(),
  206: 		event: "receive_success",
  207: 		mode: bound.mode,
  208: 		state: stateParam,
  209: 		userId: userIdParam,
  210: 	});
  211: 
  212: 	return { ok: true, authState };
  213: }
  214: 
  215: function reject(
  216: 	reason: OAuthRejectReason,
  217: 	mode?: AuthMode,
  218: 	state?: string,
  219: ): OAuthReceiveResult {
  220: 	const entry: OAuthLogEntry = {
  221: 		timestamp: Date.now(),
  222: 		event: "receive_reject",
  223: 		reason,
  224: 	};
  225: 	if (mode !== undefined) entry.mode = mode;
  226: 	if (state !== undefined) entry.state = state;
  227: 	appendLog(entry);
  228: 	return { ok: false, reason };
  229: }
  230: 
  231: /** Subscribe to forensic log events. Returns an unsubscribe function. */
  232: export function onOAuthLog(
  233: 	listener: (entry: OAuthLogEntry) => void,
  234: ): () => void {
  235: 	logListeners.add(listener);
  236: 	return () => {
  237: 		logListeners.delete(listener);
  238: 	};
  239: }
  240: 
  241: /** Snapshot copy of the in-memory forensic log buffer. */
  242: export function getOAuthLog(): readonly OAuthLogEntry[] {
  243: 	return logBuffer.slice();
  244: }

  130: /// Start a background thread that watches for deep link URLs written to a
  131: /// pending file by a second instance (see main.rs).  This is needed because
  132: /// Chromium browsers launch the protocol handler in a sandboxed context where
  133: /// the single-instance Named Mutex IPC fails silently.
  134: pub(crate) fn start_deep_link_file_watcher(app_handle: tauri::AppHandle) {
  135:     std::thread::spawn(move || {
  136:         let pending_path = dirs::home_dir()
  137:             .map(|h| h.join(".naia").join("deep-link-pending.txt"))
  138:             .unwrap_or_else(|| PathBuf::from(r"C:\Users\Public\.naia\deep-link-pending.txt"));
  139:         loop {
  140:             std::thread::sleep(std::time::Duration::from_millis(500));
  141:             if pending_path.exists() {
  142:                 if let Ok(raw) = std::fs::read_to_string(&pending_path) {
  143:                     let _ = std::fs::remove_file(&pending_path);
  144:                     let url_str = raw.trim();
  145:                     if !url_str.is_empty() {
  146:                         crate::process_deep_link_url(url_str, &app_handle, None, "file");
  147:                     }
  148:                 }
  149:             }
  150:         }

  155:             }
  156:         }
  157:         Err("No Chrome window found".to_string())
  158:     })

  161: /// Resolve tsx as a direct node invocation from agent's node_modules.

  163: ///
  164: /// Mirrors the Windows implementation so `spawn_agent_core` has one cross-platform
  165: /// code path. Using node directly avoids `npx`'s shell lookup entirely.
  166: pub(crate) fn resolve_tsx_from_agent(agent_dir: &std::path::Path) -> Option<(String, String)> {
  167:     let pnpm_dir = agent_dir.join("node_modules").join(".pnpm");

  174:                         .path()

  176:                         .join("tsx")
  177:                         .join("dist")

    1: // Typed wrappers around the naia-agent stdio IPC handlers introduced in
    2: // Phase 5a of #337. Each request/response is correlated via an `id` field on
    3: // the wire; the response arrives as a Tauri `agent_response` event because the
    4: // agent's stdout is forwarded verbatim by src-tauri/src/lib.rs:1189
    5: // (`handle.emit("agent_response", trimmed)`).
    6: //
    7: // Pattern choice (per Phase 5b spec): (B) fire-and-listen ??register a
    8: // `listen("agent_response", ...)` filter on `id`, then `invoke(
    9: // "send_to_agent_command", ...)` to write the request. Matches every existing
   10: // IPC consumer in shell/src/lib (chat-service.ts, panel-loader.ts, etc.) and
   11: // keeps the Rust side untouched apart from a separate single-field addition
   12: // to the `naia_auth_complete` payload (deepLinkUrl).
   13: //
   14: // Event subscribers (`onAgentAuthChanged`, `onAgentAuthExpired`) handle the
   15: // agent ??shell push events (`auth_changed`, `auth_expired`) that flow without
   16: // a prior request.
   17: //
   18: // All wrappers throw on transport failure (invoke rejection or response
   19: // timeout). Callers are expected to catch and surface UI-level errors.
   20: 
   21: import { invoke } from "@tauri-apps/api/core";
   22: import { listen } from "@tauri-apps/api/event";
   23: 
   24: import { Logger } from "./logger";

   83: /** Default timeout for an agent request/response round-trip (ms). */
   84: const REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS = 15_000;
   85: 
   86: let nextRequestSeq = 0;
   87: 
   88: function newRequestId(prefix: string): string {
   89: 	nextRequestSeq += 1;
   90: 	return `${prefix}-${Date.now()}-${nextRequestSeq.toString(36)}`;
   91: }

   93: interface AgentResponseLike {
   94: 	type?: string;
   95: 	id?: string;
   96: 	[k: string]: unknown;
   97: }
   98: 
   99: function parseAgentResponse(payload: unknown): AgentResponseLike | null {
  100: 	try {
  101: 		const raw = typeof payload === "string" ? payload : JSON.stringify(payload);
  102: 		const parsed = JSON.parse(raw) as unknown;
  103: 		if (parsed && typeof parsed === "object" && !Array.isArray(parsed)) {
  104: 			return parsed as AgentResponseLike;
  105: 		}
  106: 		return null;
  107: 	} catch {
  108: 		return null;
  109: 	}
  110: }
  111: 
  112: /**
  113:  * Send a JSON-encoded request to the agent and await the matching response by
  114:  * (`responseType`, `id`). The listener is unregistered as soon as the response
  115:  * arrives or the timeout fires ??never leaks across requests.
  116:  */
  117: async function requestAgent<T>(opts: {
  118: 	request: Record<string, unknown>;
  119: 	responseType: string;
  120: 	id: string;
  121: 	timeoutMs?: number;
  122: }): Promise<T> {
  123: 	const timeout = opts.timeoutMs ?? REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS;
  124: 
  125: 	let unlistenFn: (() => void) | null = null;
  126: 	let timerId: ReturnType<typeof setTimeout> | null = null;
  127: 	let settled = false;
  128: 
  129: 	const result = new Promise<T>((resolve, reject) => {
  130: 		const settleOk = (value: T) => {
  131: 			if (settled) return;
  132: 			settled = true;
  133: 			if (timerId) clearTimeout(timerId);
  134: 			if (unlistenFn) unlistenFn();
  135: 			resolve(value);
  136: 		};
  137: 		const settleErr = (err: unknown) => {
  138: 			if (settled) return;
  139: 			settled = true;
  140: 			if (timerId) clearTimeout(timerId);
  141: 			if (unlistenFn) unlistenFn();
  142: 			reject(err instanceof Error ? err : new Error(String(err)));
  143: 		};
  144: 
  145: 		timerId = setTimeout(
  146: 			() =>
  147: 				settleErr(
  148: 					new Error(`agent-ipc timeout: ${opts.responseType} id=${opts.id}`),
  149: 				),
  150: 			timeout,
  151: 		);
  152: 
  153: 		// Register listener BEFORE invoking ??same ordering as chat-service.ts:142
  154: 		// to avoid a race where the agent answers faster than the JS event loop.
  155: 		listen<string>("agent_response", (event) => {
  156: 			const parsed = parseAgentResponse(event.payload);
  157: 			if (!parsed) return;
  158: 			if (parsed.type !== opts.responseType) return;
  159: 			if (parsed.id !== opts.id) return;
  160: 			settleOk(parsed as unknown as T);
  161: 		})
  162: 			.then((fn) => {
  163: 				unlistenFn = fn;
  164: 				if (settled) {
  165: 					// Race: response/timeout arrived before listen resolved.
  166: 					fn();
  167: 					return;
  168: 				}
  169: 				invoke("send_to_agent_command", {
  170: 					message: JSON.stringify(opts.request),
  171: 				}).catch((err) => settleErr(err));
  172: 			})
  173: 			.catch((err) => settleErr(err));
  174: 	});
  175: 
  176: 	return result;
  177: }

  179: export async function agentAuthStart(opts: {
  180: 	mode: AuthMode;
  181: 	scope?: string[];
  182: 	locale?: string;
  183: }): Promise<AgentAuthStartResult> {
  184: 	const id = newRequestId("auth-start");
  185: 	const request: Record<string, unknown> = {
  186: 		type: "auth_start",
  187: 		id,
  188: 		mode: opts.mode,
  189: 	};
  190: 	if (opts.scope !== undefined) request.scope = opts.scope;
  191: 	if (opts.locale !== undefined) request.locale = opts.locale;
  192: 
  193: 	type Wire = AgentAuthStartResult & { error?: string };
  194: 	const resp = await requestAgent<Wire>({
  195: 		request,
  196: 		responseType: "auth_start_response",
  197: 		id,
  198: 	});
  199: 	if (resp.error) {
  200: 		throw new Error(`auth_start failed: ${resp.error}`);
  201: 	}
  202: 	if (typeof resp.authUrl !== "string" || typeof resp.state !== "string") {
  203: 		throw new Error("auth_start_response missing authUrl/state");
  204: 	}
  205: 	return { authUrl: resp.authUrl, state: resp.state };
  206: }
  207: 
  208: export async function agentAuthReceived(
  209: 	deepLinkUrl: string,
  210: ): Promise<AgentAuthReceivedResult> {
  211: 	const id = newRequestId("auth-received");
  212: 	const request: Record<string, unknown> = {
  213: 		type: "auth_received",
  214: 		id,
  215: 		deepLinkUrl,
  216: 	};
  217: 	type Wire = AgentAuthReceivedResult & { error?: string };
  218: 	const resp = await requestAgent<Wire>({
  219: 		request,
  220: 		responseType: "auth_received_response",
  221: 		id,
  222: 	});
  223: 	// `error` is a transport/parser-level fault from the agent dispatcher.
  224: 	// `reason` is a structured rejection (state mismatch, expired, etc.).
  225: 	// Both flatten into the same `ok: false` shape for callers.
  226: 	const out: AgentAuthReceivedResult = { ok: resp.ok === true };
  227: 	if (!out.ok) {
  228: 		if (typeof resp.reason === "string") out.reason = resp.reason;
  229: 		else if (typeof resp.error === "string") out.reason = resp.error;
  230: 	}
  231: 	if (typeof resp.userId === "string") out.userId = resp.userId;
  232: 	if (resp.mode === "dev" || resp.mode === "prod") out.mode = resp.mode;
  233: 	return out;
  234: }

  236: export async function agentAuthLogout(mode: AuthMode): Promise<void> {
  237: 	const id = newRequestId("auth-logout");
  238: 	const request = { type: "auth_logout", id, mode };
  239: 	await requestAgent<{ ok: true }>({
  240: 		request,
  241: 		responseType: "auth_logout_response",
  242: 		id,
  243: 	});
  244: }

   21: /// Cross-platform home directory: HOME (Unix) or USERPROFILE (Windows).
   22: pub(crate) fn home_dir() -> String {
   23:     std::env::var("HOME")
   24:         .or_else(|_| std::env::var("USERPROFILE"))
   25:         .unwrap_or_default()
   26: }
   27: 
   28: fn is_valid_gateway_key(value: &str) -> bool {
   29:     value.starts_with("gw-")
   30:         && value.len() <= 256
   31:         && value
   32:             .chars()
   33:             .all(|c| c.is_alphanumeric() || c == '-' || c == '_')
   34: }
   35: 
   36: /// Process a deep-link URL (naia://auth?key=xxx). Extracted as a function
   37: /// so both the Tauri deep-link plugin callback and the Windows file watcher
   38: /// can share the same parsing + validation logic.
   39: pub(crate) fn process_deep_link_url(
   40:     url_str: &str,
   41:     app_handle: &AppHandle,
   42:     oauth_state: Option<&Arc<Mutex<Option<String>>>>,
   43:     source: &str,
   44: ) {
   45:     let redacted = url_str.split('?').next().unwrap_or(url_str);
   46:     log_both(&format!(
   47:         "[Naia] Deep link received ({}): {}?[REDACTED]",
   48:         source, redacted
   49:     ));
   50:     let parsed = match url::Url::parse(url_str) {
   51:         Ok(u) => u,
   52:         Err(_) => return,
   53:     };
   54:     if parsed.host_str() != Some("auth") && parsed.path() != "auth" && parsed.path() != "/auth" {
   55:         return;
   56:     }
   57:     let mut key = None;
   58:     let mut code = None;
   59:     let mut user_id = None;
   60:     let mut incoming_state = None;
   61:     let mut channel = None;
   62:     let mut discord_user_id = None;
   63:     let mut discord_channel_id = None;
   64:     let mut discord_target = None;
   65:     for (k, v) in parsed.query_pairs() {
   66:         match k.as_ref() {
   67:             "key" => key = Some(v.to_string()),
   68:             "code" => code = Some(v.to_string()),
   69:             "user_id" => user_id = Some(v.to_string()),
   70:             "state" => incoming_state = Some(v.to_string()),
   71:             "channel" => channel = Some(v.to_string()),
   72:             "discord_user_id" | "discordUserId" => discord_user_id = Some(v.to_string()),
   73:             "discord_channel_id" | "discordChannelId" => discord_channel_id = Some(v.to_string()),
   74:             "discord_target" | "discordTarget" => discord_target = Some(v.to_string()),
   75:             _ => {}
   76:         }
   77:     }
   78:     let has_direct_gateway_key = key.as_deref().is_some_and(is_valid_gateway_key)
   79:         || code.as_deref().is_some_and(is_valid_gateway_key);
   80:     if let Some(state_mutex) = oauth_state {
  520:                         let guard_result = state.gateway.lock();
  521:                         if let Ok(mut guard) = guard_result {
  522:                             // Kill existing if any
  523:                             if let Some(mut old) = guard.take() {
  524:                                 if let Some(ref mut nh) = old.node_host {
  525:                                     let _ = nh.kill();
  526:                                 }
  527:                                 if old.we_spawned {
  528:                                     let _ = old.child.kill();
  529:                                 }
  530:                             }
  531:                             // Try to respawn
  532:                             match spawn_gateway() {
  533:                                 Ok(process) => {
  534:                                     let managed = process.we_spawned;
  535:                                     *guard = Some(process);
  536:                                     Some(managed)
  537:                                 }
  538:                                 Err(e) => {
  539:                                     log_both(&format!("[Naia] Gateway restart failed: {}", e));
  540:                                     None
  541:                                 }
  542:                             }
  543:                         } else {
  544:                             None
  545:                         }
  546:                     };
  547:                     if let Some(managed) = restart_result {
  548:                         consecutive_failures = 0;
  549:                         log_both(&format!("[Naia] Gateway restarted (managed={})", managed));
  550:                         let _ = app_handle.emit(
  551:                             "gateway_status",
  552:                             serde_json::json!({
  553:                                 "running": true,
  554:                                 "managed": managed,
  555:                                 "restarted": true
  556:                             }),
  557:                         );
  558:                     }
  559:                 }
  560:             }
  561:         }
  562:     });
  563:     shutdown
  564: }
  565: 
  566: /// Run `<node> -v` with a hidden console and return the parsed major version.
  567: ///
  568: /// On Windows GUI apps (no console), `Command::output()` without CREATE_NO_WINDOW
  569: /// triggers `ERROR_NO_DATA (0x800700e8)` ??"The pipe is being closed" ??because
  570: /// Rust cannot attach the child's stdio to a non-existent console. `hide_console`
  571: /// sets `CREATE_NO_WINDOW` (no-op on Unix), which fixes the pipe setup.
  572: fn node_major_version<P: AsRef<std::ffi::OsStr>>(node_path: P) -> Option<u32> {
  573:     let mut cmd = Command::new(node_path);
  574:     cmd.arg("-v");
  575:     platform::hide_console(&mut cmd);
  576:     let output = cmd.output().ok()?;
  577:     if !output.status.success() {
  578:         return None;
  579:     }
  580:     String::from_utf8_lossy(&output.stdout)
  581:         .trim()
  582:         .trim_start_matches('v')
  583:         .split('.')
  584:         .next()
  585:         .and_then(|s| s.parse().ok())
  586: }
  587: 
  588: /// Find Node.js binary (system path first, then nvm fallback)
  589: fn find_node_binary() -> Result<std::path::PathBuf, String> {
  590:     // Flatpak bundled node (Linux only)
  591:     #[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
  592:     {
  593:         let flatpak_node = std::path::PathBuf::from("/app/bin/node");
  594:         if flatpak_node.exists() {
  595:             return Ok(flatpak_node);
  596:         }
  597:     }
  598: 
  599:     // Check system node first
  600:     let node_cmd = if cfg!(windows) { "node.exe" } else { "node" };
  601:     if let Some(major) = node_major_version(node_cmd) {
  602:         if major >= 22 {
  603:             return Ok(std::path::PathBuf::from(node_cmd));
  604:         }
  605:     }
  606: 
  607:     let home = home_dir();
  608: 
  609:     // Windows: check nvm-windows, fnm, and Program Files
  610:     #[cfg(windows)]
  611:     {
  612:         // nvm-windows (NVM_HOME or default AppData\Roaming\nvm)
  613:         let nvm_home = std::env::var("NVM_HOME")
  614:             .unwrap_or_else(|_| format!("{}\\AppData\\Roaming\\nvm", home));
  615:         // fnm (actual installations, not ephemeral multishells)
  616:         let fnm_dir = format!("{}\\AppData\\Local\\fnm_multishells", home);
  617:         let win_dirs = [nvm_home, fnm_dir];
  618:         for dir in &win_dirs {
  619:             if let Ok(entries) = std::fs::read_dir(dir) {
  620:                 for entry in entries.flatten() {

    7: export function buildNaiaAuthDeepLink(input: BuildNaiaAuthDeepLinkInput): string {
    8:   const params = new URLSearchParams();
    9:   params.set("key", input.key);
   10: 
   11:   if (input.userId?.trim()) {
   12:     params.set("user_id", input.userId.trim());
   13:   }

   15:   if (input.state?.trim()) {

   18:

   20: }
   21: 
   22: /**
   23:  * Build an HTTPS callback URL for embedded Chrome.
   24:  * The Naia desktop app monitors URL changes via CDP and extracts the key
   25:  * from this URL pattern, avoiding the need for custom scheme deep links
   26:  * which don't work inside embedded Chrome.
   27:  */
   28: export function buildDesktopAuthCallbackUrl(
   29:   input: BuildNaiaAuthDeepLinkInput,
   30: ): string {
   31:   const params = new URLSearchParams();
   32:   params.set("key", input.key);
   33: 
   34:   if (input.userId?.trim()) {
   35:     params.set("user_id", input.userId.trim());
   36:   }
   37: 
   38:   if (input.state?.trim()) {
   39:     params.set("state", input.state.trim());
   40:   }
   41: 
   42:   const origin = typeof window !== "undefined" ? window.location.origin : "https://naia.nextain.io";
   43:   return `${origin}/desktop/auth-complete?${params.toString()}`;
   44: }
